WELL EVALUATION
Figure 1: The H&P 471 at the Marathon Oil Co. Greider 34-20TFH well,
July of 2014, 5 miles northeast of Dunn Center in Dunn County County, ND.
(Photos by K. Kouri, Geologist)
INTRODUCTION
The Marathon Oil Company - Greider 34-20TFH well is located approximately 5 miles
northeast of Dunn Center in Dunn County, North Dakota [Section 29, T46N, R93W]. The
subject well was drilled by H&P rig 471 within Bailey Field (Figure 1). The well was planned
for one approximately 10,000' long lateral well-bore to be drilled in the Devonian, Three Forks
Formation. The Three Forks target was defined as a ten foot thick section with intent to intersect
porous horizons and natural fracture trends that could enhance reservoir quality.
OFFSET CONTROL INFORMATION
Three offset wells were used to develop a well rounded prognosis and identify formation tops
and structure trends. The three offset wells utilized included:
(1) Marathon Oil Company's Brink 24-20TFH [NW NE 29-T146N-R93W] which lies
approximately 100' west, and was drilled in July of 2014 in the Three Forks Formation (Fig. 2).
(2) Marathon Oil Company's Evelyn 34-32TFH [SW SE 32-T146N-R93W] which lies
approximately 2 miles south, and was drilled in April of 2013 in Three Forks Formation.
(3) Marathon Oil Company's Hansen Ranch 44-10TFH [SE SE 10-T146N-R93W] which lies
approximately 2.5 miles northeast, and was drilled in January of 2010 in the Three Forks
Formation.
All three offset wells were used in correlation of Lodgepole, Bakken and Three Forks markers as
the curve progressed. A successful curve landing was accomplished at 10,630' TVD. Multiple
other offset wells were used for structure control during the lateral, including the Lucy
Fleckenstein 34-20H and Castner 34-20H (Figure 2).
ENGINEERING
On the morning of September 05, 2014 the well was spud drilling a 13½" hole with freshwater to
2,178' MD, where the well-bore was isolated with 9 " casing (10,955') & cemented to surface.
From 2,178' MD, diesel invert drilling fluid was used throughout the remaining vertical and
curve build sections, maintaining a 9.7-10.25 (ppg) mud weight for stable-hole conditions. An 8
¾" bottom-hole assembly (BHA) was picked up and drilling continued to 8,143' MD where a bit
trip was necessary due to slowing penetration rates. The bit was changed out and drilling
continued, just prior to kick-off point at 10,104' MD.
The curve assembly consisted of an 8 ¾" bit, 2.35° mud motor and gamma & survey tools.
Rotary drilling continued to 10,120' MD, where the desired kick-off point was reached. At
KOP, the well was drilled down to 10,974' MD where the resultant curve was landed at 10,630'
TVD in the lower half of the defined target zone. Directional tools were then pulled out of the
hole and a string of 7" casing was set (11,955' MD) and then cemented by Schlumberger after
which true lateral operations commenced.
At 10,974' MD, a 6" bit, 1.50º mud motor and MWD tools comprised the first lateral BHA and
were run in the hole on 4" drill pipe. The lateral drilled until 13,028' when ROP slowed down
and a trip was made for the BHA. Once back to bottom, drilling continued until 17,444' MD
when ROP slowed and another trip was needed. Once the BHA was changed out, drilling
continued until a total depth of 21,018' MD. The lateral resulted in a total depth of 21,018' MD
(10,646.92' TVD), at a final closure distance of 10,799.98' resulting in a closure direction of
359.70º. The bottom-hole location is: 10,799.83' north and 57.00' west of surface location or
approximately 211.23' from the north line and 2,207.00' from the east line in northwest quadrant
of the northeast quarter of Section 17, T146N and R93W (Figure 2).

GEOLOGIC EVALUATION
Methods:
Geologic supervision was provided by Sunburst Consulting, Inc. with two well-site geologists.
A digital gas detector and chromatograph were interfaced with a NOV Rig Sense electronic data
recorder system. The Rig Sense provided drill rate, on-off bottom and pump strokes to the gas
detection computer and received total gas information from Sunburst for viewing around
location. Lagged samples were caught in 30' intervals from 8,200' to a total depth of 21,018'.
Wet and dry cuttings were examined under a binocular microscope and complete lithologic
descriptions and sampling intervals are provided in the lithology document within this
evaluation. Two sets of dry cuttings were collected during the duration of the well.
Generalized Stratigraphy and Zones of Interest:
The upper Kibbey Formation is composed predominately of siltstone with intermittent sections
of silty sandstone. The siltstone through this interval is mottled red-brown to light gray and
cream in color, soft, very fine grained and calcite cemented. The silty sandstone sections were
white to clear and light pink to orange-tan. It was medium to coarse grained, sub-rounded to sub-
angular, moderately sorted and composed primarily of quartz grains loosely cemented by calcite.
A persistent limestone bed in the middle of the unit is known as the Kibbey "Lime", penetrated
at 8,282' TVD (-5,946'), and is represented by a fine to microcrystalline, friable to firm, gray to
brown lime mudstone. The lower Kibbey exhibits lithology similar to that of the upper but the
siltstone has an increasing anhydritic content towards the base.
The first salt, representing the top of the Charles Formation, in this area, was penetrated at
8,433' TVD (-6,097'). Other salt beds encountered intermittently for the next 497 feet, where the
Base of the Last Salt was drilled at 8,930' TVD (-6,594'). A cyclical depositional sequence also
deposited anhydrite and limestone throughout the Charles Formation. The anhydrite was
generally white to gray in color and soft to slightly firm. The limestone was off white to gray in
color, very fine to microcrystalline with a crystalline to slightly chalky texture. The prospective
Ratcliffe interval was drilled at 8,869' TVD (-6,533') and consisted of argillaceous limestone
and dolomite. The mudstone and occasional wackestone, within the Ratcliffe, had fine traces of
visible intercrystalline porosity but no visible oil stain.
The top of the Mission Canyon Formation
was drilled at 9,106' TVD (-6,770') and
consists primarily of limestone interbedded
with dolomitic limestone. The dolomitic
limestone within the Mission Canyon is a
gray to brown, fine crystalline, soft to
friable mudstone to wackestone, and
showed rare traces of intercrystalline
porosity (Figure 3).
Figure 3: Mission Canyon limestone.
A transition to argillaceous limestone, signifying the top of the Lodgepole Formation, was
penetrated at 9,660' MD, 9,656' TVD (-7,320'). A normal platform to slope marine environment
deposited approximately 851' of consistent gray to light gray-brown, microcrystalline,
argillaceous mudstone. An excellent subinterval in the lower Lodgepole is known as the False
Bakken, drilled at 10,583' MD; 10,507' TVD (-8,171'), and consisted of a dark brown,
calcareous, earthy shale that was soft to friable and contained common disseminated pyrite.
The Upper Bakken Shale Member, signifying the top of the Bakken Formation, was penetrated
at 10,617' MD, 10,531' TVD (-8,195'), and consisted of petroliferous and carbonaceous black
shale (Figure 4). The Middle Bakken Member was penetrated at 10,647' MD, 10,546' TVD (-
8,210'). The middle member consisted of a varying thickness and sequence of inter-bedded
siltstone, limestone and silty sandstone. The dominant light gray to light gray-brown, fine
grained, calcite cemented silty sandstone contained traces of disseminated pyrite, rare nodular
pyrite and spotty light brown oil staining. The Lower Bakken Shale Member was penetrated at
10,725' MD, 10,583' TVD (-8,247'). The lower shale is similar to the upper shale: black, friable
to firm, blocky, earthy texture, petroliferous, carbonaceous, common disseminated and nodular
pyrite, even oil stain (Figure 5). The Pronghorn Member was penetrated at 10,763' MD and
10,598' TVD (-8,262'). It is a siltstone described as: light to medium gray-brown, occasional
cream to off white, very fine grained, friable, sub-angular, moderately sorted, calcite cemented,
trace disseminated pyrite, trace intergranular porosity, and trace light brown spotty oil stain.
Figure 4 & 5: Upper Bakken shale (left) and lower Bakken shale (right).
The targeted Three Forks Formation was penetrated at 10,783' MD, 10,604' TVD (-8,268').
Samples consist of a mix of pale green to pale blue green shale and tan to cream dolomite
(Figure 6). The dolomite showed traces of intercrystalline porosity and spotty, light brown oil
staining. Areas are known to have disseminated pyrite with some nodular pyrite.
Figure 6: Three Forks, dolomite and shale from the defined target zone.
Lateral Geology
Geo-steering:
Baker Hughes Inteq provided the directional drilling operations and equipment and personnel for
MWD services. The directional drillers and Sunburst geologists worked closely together
throughout the project to make steering decisions to maximize the amount of borehole exposure
to pay zone for the lateral section.
Samples from the target zone varied in porosity, oil staining, color, cementation, and pyrite
content. Stratigraphic location in the target zone was based on these sample observations along
with gas shows, drill rates and gamma ray values.
The proposed target was defined as the central 10' of the upper Three Forks. The target zone
was bounded by a gamma signature upwards of 60 counts at the top, a semi-`ratty' 60-100 count
gamma in the target zone, before decreasing to below 65 counts and increasing to over 130
counts in the definitive chocolate dolomite (Figure 7).

Figure 7: Offset well (MOC O'Neil Vertical) with gamma ray values (0-200 API) & target settings, overlaid with
curve landing gamma from Greider 34-20TFH.
*See subsequent dip profile (Figure 8) presentation*
Lateral drilling began in the lower half of the defined target zone. After drilling through cement,
the well-bore was brought back above perceived dip and ascended through the target, eventually
tagging the top of target. Here, a 0.10° down dip was calculated. At this point the well-bore was
slowly brought back down to the "H" marker base of target and a dip of 0.21° down was
calculated. At this point, structure trends closely resembled the Brink 24-20TFH, drilled 100'
west on this same pad. As drilling continued a 0.30° down dip was calculated as the well-bore
went slightly below the base of target and back into target tagging the bottom of the "H" marker.
This 0.30° down dip flattened slightly to a 0.25° down-dip. At this point the well-bore fell into
the cooler, "K" gamma marker and eventually into the chocolate dolomite marker at ~15,900'
MD. Assuming the structural dip was still down the well-bore was brought slightly above an
inclination of 90 degrees assuming the well would exit the lower dolomite quickly. The well
failed to exit the lower dolomite, so upward slides were initiated and the well successfully drilled
out of the lower dolomite at 17,150' MD, resulting in an unexpected dip reversal of 0.49° up-dip.
At this point in the lateral the up dip did not match any of the surrounding offset wells. Drilling
continued, and a brief encounter with the chocolate dolomite once again resulted in a 0.03° up-
dip. The well drilled up section, along a newly proposed 0.21° up-dip before finally observing
an expected return to a down dipping structure at ~19,081' MD. A -0.33° was calculated for the
remainder of the lateral.
Using the above information gathered during drilling, offset log information and the structural
data provided from Marathon Oil Company geologists, well-site geologists were able to
anticipate, interpret and adjust the dip rates during the drilling of the Greider 34-20TFH.. A total
depth of 21,018' MD was reached on September 20, 2014 at 13:41 MT. The target resultant was
40% within the targeted interval and 100% within the Three Forks Formation. The resulting
structure of formation was a drop in TVD of 14.00 feet over 10,255', resulting in a gross
apparent down-dip of 0.08º as portrayed on the Greider 34-20TFH dip profile (Figure 8).

Hydrocarbons:
Background gas, out of casing started below 500 units. As drilling progressed to 11,400' MD,
gas increased to 500 to 2,000 units by 12,300' MD. After a trip at 13,068' MD, gas decreased
below 750 units until the well-bore climbed out of the chocolate dolomite at 17,120' MD. Here,
gas values increased 250 to 1,500 units. At 19,200' MD, gas again decreased to below 500 units
(Figure 9). At this time the rig started to vent through the gas buster, and 20 gallons of drilling
lubricants and other chemicals were added each stand of drill pipe. It is thought that these
chemicals were a reason for the lower gas count. The gas equipment was continuously checked
to ensure it was working properly.
No backside, casing pressure was held during drilling, and the only flare was seen on the trip at
17,444' MD. At this trip, the trip gas measured 2,389 units and a 45' trip flare was observed-no
other flares were observed while drilling.

SUMMARY
· The Helmerich & Payne drilling rig #471 successfully drilled a two-section, horizontal
well-bore within the Three Forks Formation, at the Marathon Oil Company: Greider 34-
20TFH. A net of 10,255' was drilled within the Three Forks Formation.
· A mud program consisting of diesel invert (9.70­10.25 ppg) was used during the vertical
and curve build sections, and saltwater was used (9.70-9.90 ppg) during the lateral which
maintained stable-hole conditions and permitted adequate analysis of gas concentrations.
· Steering was accomplished by sample evaluation, following correlative drilling rates and
MWD gamma-ray markers, and making dip estimations based on the intersection of these
markers. Projections of dip were successfully used to maintain the well-bore 100%
within the Three Forks Formation, and 40% within the Marathon defined target interval.
· Samples from the target consisted of dolomite with fine intercrystalline porosity and
spotty light brown oil staining, interbedded with light pale green-pale blue green shale.
· The Greider 34-20TFH will be fitted with a 4 ½" production liner in preparation for a
multi-stage fracture stimulation that will determine the true commercial value of the well.
The well currently awaits fracture stimulation.
Respectfully submitted,
Kyle Kouri
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
September 22 2014

Lithology
Rig crews caught lagged samples in 30' intervals, under the supervision of a Sunburst geologist. A detailed list of
sampling intervals is included in the well data summary page. Sample or gamma-ray marker tops have been inserted in
the sample descriptions below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular microscope.
Sample descriptions began in the Kibbey Formation and ended in the Three Forks Formation. Drilling fluid was fresh-
water for surface, oil based for intermediate and salt-water to conclusion of the lateral.
Kibbey "Lime"
8,286' MD 8,282' TVD (-5,946')
8200-8230 SILTSTONE: red to red-brown, common orange-red, friable, sub-blocky, calcite cemented, moderately
cemented, possible intergranular porosity; occasional SHALE: orange-brown to red-orange, friable, sub-blocky, earthy
texture
8230-8260 SILTSTONE to SHALE: orange-brown to red-orange, occasional orange-brown, friable to rare soft in part,
sub-blocky, calcite cemented, poorly cemented, possible intergranular porosity; rare ANHYDRITE: off white to cream,
soft, amorphous, earthy texture, no visible porosity
8260-8290 SILTSTONE: light red-brown, occasional off white, friable to soft, sub-rounded, calcite cemented,
moderately cemented, possible intergranular porosity; rare ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy
texture, no visible porosity
8290-8320 SILTSTONE: light to medium red-brown, occasional off white, friable, sub-rounded, calcite cemented,
moderately cemented, possible intergranular porosity; occasional LIMESTONE: mudstone, light tan to gray,
microcrystalline, firm, no visible porosity; common ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy texture,
no visible porosity
8320-8350 LIMESTONE: mudstone, light beige to light gray, microcrystalline to very fine crystalline, firm to hard, no
visible porosity; rare ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy texture, no visible porosity
8350-8380 SILTSTONE: light tan to light red-brown, friable to hard, sub-rounded, calcite cemented, moderately
cemented, possible intergranular porosity, trace ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy texture, no
visible porosity
8380-8410 SILTSTONE: light beige to light red-brown, firm to hard, sub-rounded, calcite cemented, moderately
cemented, possible intergranular porosity; common ANHYDRITE: cream to off white, soft, amorphous, earthy texture,
no visible porosity; common SALT: translucent to clear, hard, euhedral to subhedral, crystalline texture

HORIZONTAL WELL

Well File # 28704
Dear William:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 24406, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200'
setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the 1280 acre
spacing unit consisting of Sections 17 & 20 T146N R93W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter
sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site
during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. In cases where a
spacing unit is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an affidavit must be provided affirming that the surface
owner of the multi-well pad agrees to accept burial on their property of the cuttings generated from drilling
the well(s) into an offsite spacing unit. Marathon may set conductor on permitted wells only. MARATHON
OIL CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Ashleigh Devenberg at
701-290-3277 prior to location
construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling
and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent
pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are
prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill
cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is:
625 N. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10807
N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be
waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to
evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that
would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the
applicant should retain the permit.
William F Groffy
June 23, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck,
via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number, drilling
contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m.
to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must
be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the
directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the
director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a
certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or
when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is hereby
granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing on the date
the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well records
wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall permit the
Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or controlled by them,
complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to have access at all times to
any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect producing and drilling wells. Any
information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time upon request. The information so
obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and shall be available only to the Commission
and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours,
and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the
plug or initiating tests.
Logs
NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well
bore, and (3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic
cement evaluation log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior
to completing the well. All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format)
copy and one digital LAS (log ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or
attached to an email sent to digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.

Engineering Technician

Surveys are required at least every 30 feet in the build section and every 90 feet in the lateral section of a horizontal well. Measurement
inaccuracies are not considered when determining compliance with the spacing/drilling unit boundary setback requirement except in the

methods and equipment are not utilized. Consult the applicable field order for exceptions.

BAKKEN
DEVELOPMENT
Engineering Technician
April 9, 2014
RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Marathon Oil Company

1.
BOP EQUIPMENT
Marathon Oil Company's minimum specifications for pressure
control equipment are as follows:
Ram Type:
13 5/8" 5000 psi blind, pipe and annular.
a. Due to Marathon's experience it is felt that the above
referenced BOP equipment is adequate for drilling this well.
The reduced permeability of the target zone along with
Marathon's area experience of drilling over 250 horizontal
wells indicate that a MASP of 3000 psi is more adjusted to
the reality of the reservoir.
BOP and other equipment testing:
a. Floor valve, dart valve, kill valves, check valve, manual
choke line valve, manual top drive valve, hydraulic top
drive valve, HCR, choke house valves, choke manifold,
choke hose, choke line, kill line, upper pipe rams, lower
pipe rams, blind rams (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High
Test: 5000 psi x 10 min.)
b. Annular Preventer (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min. High Test:
2500 psi x 10 min.)
c. Rotating head and Orbit Valve (Low Test: 250 psi x 5 min.
High Test: 1500 psi x 10 min.)
Frequency:
a. After initial installation (NU BOPE).
b. Whenever any seal subject to test pressure is broken.
c. After any repairs compromising seal.
d. At 30-day intervals.
All other equipment (upper and lower Kelly cocks, IBOP,
etc) will be tested according to Onshore Oil and Gas
Order No. 2.

b. Marathon will maintain 1000 sxs of barite on location.
This allows weighting up from 10.0 ppg to 14.5 ppg of 325
bbls of fluid, such that 10,000 ft of vertical annulus
can be displaced with kill mud.
c. Pits are monitored through an EDR system utilizing floats
and alarms to monitor abnormal volume gains or losses.
4.
EVALUATION PROGRAM
The anticipated type and amount of testing, logging and coring
are as follows:
a. The logging program will consist of the following:
i. Waiver is attached not to run logs except those
shown below.
ii. CBL to be run above cement top and a GR back to
surface.
iii. Curve will be drilled with MWD including GR to
intermediate casing point.
b. Mud logging services will commence prior to penetrating
below (base of Charles salt):
i. Samples will be obtained at 10' intervals to
intermediate casing point and at 30' intervals below
intermediate to TD.
c. No drill stem tests are anticipated.

d. Well will be fracture stimulated and placed on

5.
ABNORMAL PRESSURES AND H2S GAS
a. The maximum anticipated bottom-hole pressure is 7810 psi.
Abnormal pressures are not anticipated.
b. Potential exists for hydrogen sulfide gas in the Madison.
6.
Well Completion
a. A 4 ½" liner will be run from above the 7" casing shoe to
the bottom of the well.
Liner has frac sleeves
installed.
b. Tie back liner will be run from top of 4 ½" Liner back to
the surface.
c. Well will be fractured utilizing a 30 stage frac.
d. Pursuant to NDIC letter effective February 12,2014,
concerning Hydraulic Fracture Stimulation using Diesel
Fuels, Marathon Oil Company will not inject diesel fuel
or any diesel-type chemicals (68334-30-5, 68476-34-6,
68476-30-2, 68476-31-3, or 8008-20-6) during the
hydraulic fracture stimulation process or this well.
Marathon understands the guidelines that are outline in
the above referenced letter including the requirement to
obtain an Underground Injection Control, Class II permit
from the NDIC prior to commencing any Hydraulic Fracture
Stimulation in which any amount of diesel fuel or any
diesel type chemical is injected.

Gas Capture Plan
Greider 34-20TFH
Sec 29 T146N R93W
Field: Bailey
Flowback Strategy
Anticipated First Production date
The Greider 34-20TFH is expected to commence production around January 2015. It is anticipated that it will be
connected to a gas sales pipeline at first production.
Multi-well startup
The well is expected to flowback concurrently with one of the other wells on the Krebs location. Flowback of the
well is expected to be approximately 4-10 days in duration.
Anticipated Oil and Gas Rates
Average Gas rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 500 MSCFD.
Average Gas rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 1,800 MSCFD
Average Oil Rate from the well during flowback is anticipated to be around 700 bopd
Average Oil Rate from the wellpad during flowback is anticipated to be around 2,800 bopd
System Capacity and Utilization
Existing Gas Line

Throughput (MMSCFD)

6 MMSCFD

Gas Gatherer Expansion Plans
16" line will connect Killdeer and Lost Bridge Compressor stations allowing gas to flow to Oneok Garden Creek
